<div id="review_583058066" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/583058066" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11811388-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344831655p2/11811388.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/583058066?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/11811388-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer583058066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13684871053545747725">The only other Orson Scott Card book I've ever read was Ender's Game. So I may not have the best background for determining if this was a good book or not. On the other hand, it may give the best background to determine if it was good. <br/><br/>Honestly, I liked Earth Unaware. It was full of intriguing plot-lines and characters, intense action sequences, and extremely interesting business models (space mining). Sure, it was a little far-fetched with ultra-intelligent teenagers inventing remarkably useful</span>
  <span id="freeText13684871053545747725" style="display:none">The only other Orson Scott Card book I've ever read was Ender's Game. So I may not have the best background for determining if this was a good book or not. On the other hand, it may give the best background to determine if it was good. <br /><br />Honestly, I liked Earth Unaware. It was full of intriguing plot-lines and characters, intense action sequences, and extremely interesting business models (space mining). Sure, it was a little far-fetched with ultra-intelligent teenagers inventing remarkably useful pieces of equipment for their free miner families. But wasn't Enders Game a little far-fetched in that regard as well? <br /><br />I've read reviews saying this book had a "healthy dose" of mormonism in it. I have no idea what these reviewers are talking about. Could it be that they're referring to Card's religion, or perhaps to the family values and morals of the characters in Earth Unaware? If it's the latter- I like to think of these as more traditional values without labeling them with any particular faith. Yes, Earth Unaware had these traditional family values which I found very refreshing. Many books these days seem to have a ton of sex and terrible language. So thank you Card and Johnston. <br /><br />One of my complaints were that some of the plot-lines never actually connected with that of the others. In other words, some of the characters never had any involvement with the aliens at all. So the whole time I was wondering, "why am I reading about these guys?" Fortunately, every plot-line was very cool. <br /><br />Also, and this shames me to say this, I didn't think this was going to be part of a trilogy or anything. So this story comes to a very abrupt end without any satisfying resolution other than the fact someone finally listened and believed Victor's tale of aliens at the end. So that was very anti-climactic. I suspect Lem Jukes will eventually use his gravity drill on the Formic ship, so that may be a little predictable (but I don't really know this). <br /><br />I also had a hard time relating to the main character, Victor. I never really felt an emotional connection with him. This, to me, usually determines my level of interest in reading the next books in the series. So, needless to say, I can take the next books or leave them. Most likely, I will read them too though.<br /><br />Overall, this was a good book and I would recommend it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13684871053545747725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_478627971" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478627971" />
    <a title="Annette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1426170-annette"><img alt="Annette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401252164p2/1426170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/478627971?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annette" href="/user/show/1426170-annette">Annette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1426170-annette?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer478627971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer95247880716363170">When I saw Aaron Johnston listed as co-author on this book, I was ready for it to be something of the general quality of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/234731.Invasive_Procedures' title='Invasive Procedures by Orson Scott Card' rel='nofollow noopener'>Invasive Procedures</a> - in other words, poor. Indeed, I nearly gave it up after the first few chapters because I didn't think I could handle 350 pages featuring a host of emotionally damaged, introspective characters plagued by dysfunctional family relationships - written by someone other than Card - just then. Having no other book on my "must read" list ready to hand, I stuck w</span>
  <span id="freeText95247880716363170" style="display:none">When I saw Aaron Johnston listed as co-author on this book, I was ready for it to be something of the general quality of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/234731.Invasive_Procedures" title="Invasive Procedures by Orson Scott Card" rel="nofollow noopener">Invasive Procedures</a> - in other words, poor. Indeed, I nearly gave it up after the first few chapters because I didn't think I could handle 350 pages featuring a host of emotionally damaged, introspective characters plagued by dysfunctional family relationships - written by someone other than Card - just then. Having no other book on my "must read" list ready to hand, I stuck with it, and this turned out to be a good decision. First, the characters and families are largely less emotionally damaged and dysfunctional (if not less introspective!) than the average book in the Ender universe. Second, there are enough characters (no laser-like focus on any given one here) and enough action that the effect is rather dissipated. Third, the writing, and especially the plotting, is considerably better than "Invasive Procedures," which I am tentatively ready to dismiss as an anomaly not indicative of Johnston's true capabilities. <br />Be aware that this is a multi-book series with the next volumes still unpublished, and also that it is a parallel series expanding upon (and, I suspect, occasionally contradicting) a series of Marvel-published comics - which went by completely under my own radar as graphic novels are not my genre. So if you happen to be completely new to the Ender universe, you might not want to start here... yet. I'm not willing to say the finished series Couldn't be a good intro to the universe, but you're going to want more when you finish. Might as well read them in the order published. </span>
  <a data-text-id="95247880716363170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321797384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6377798419188870433">Let me start off saying, that this is the first Orson Scott Card book that I've read (though certainly not the last), so while I had a vague notion that it was some sort of prequel thing to the Ender books, I didn't really know what it was about. Fortunately, I didn't need to know a thing. It was amazing anyway.<br/><br/>Earth Unaware follows a large and scattered group of characters through the initial discovery of the "hormigos", or Formics, when they first invade our galaxy. It's not the easiest book t</span>
  <span id="freeText6377798419188870433" style="display:none">Let me start off saying, that this is the first Orson Scott Card book that I've read (though certainly not the last), so while I had a vague notion that it was some sort of prequel thing to the Ender books, I didn't really know what it was about. Fortunately, I didn't need to know a thing. It was amazing anyway.<br /><br />Earth Unaware follows a large and scattered group of characters through the initial discovery of the "hormigos", or Formics, when they first invade our galaxy. It's not the easiest book to read, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[death abounds, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but it is fascinating none the less. The incoming alien ship tests the motives and courage of everyone they encounter as they decide what's most important to them... and how best to stay alive.<br /><br />Fascinating characters and world-building details fill this book. From little Mono, sky-watcher Edimar and lead mechanic Segundo to gamma propulsion and free mining families, I didn't want to put this book down once I picked it up. And actually... I didn't. I finished it the same day I started.<br /><br />I'm anxiously awaiting the second book of The First Formic War, and in the meantime, I'll probably be picking up Ender's Game. Don't pass this one up.<br /><br />[I received this book for free through First Reads and was not required to write a positive or any other type of review. All opinions stated herein are solely my own.]</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13587257554615411369"> <br/>Earth Unaware by Orson Scott Card and Aaron Johsnston <br/><br/>This book is a back story for Ender’s Game. If you have not read the Ender series, do so, you will not regret it. Victor is a mechanically talented young man in a mining clan thrust into the role of interstellar hero. <br/><br/>Card has the ability to create characters with utter realism. You may even think you have met some of his characters. Stretching the comparison, I was a small independent computer dealer in competition with corporate entities l</span>
  <span id="freeText13587257554615411369" style="display:none"> <br />Earth Unaware by Orson Scott Card and Aaron Johsnston <br /><br />This book is a back story for Ender’s Game. If you have not read the Ender series, do so, you will not regret it. Victor is a mechanically talented young man in a mining clan thrust into the role of interstellar hero. <br /><br />Card has the ability to create characters with utter realism. You may even think you have met some of his characters. Stretching the comparison, I was a small independent computer dealer in competition with corporate entities like Compaq, HP and Dell. I often felt the competition unfair and frustrating. In one instance I was selling IBM pcs to a community college and was underbid by IBM direct sales. Since I am a firm believer in no spoilers, you will have to read this book to see why I am reminded of the often cut-throat aspects of small business vs. big business. <br /><br />Sadly it is too long ago that I read the Ender series. The book did not resonate with those books. It did however stand alone very nicely and should entice an entire new group of readers to Ender’s story. <br /><br />The afterword, which I often don’t bother to read, provides an explanation for this book and for future and concurrent titles. Again if you haven’t read the Ender series, jump online and buy it now but read this book first. <br /><br />I recommend it. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13587257554615411369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer11120278428688743946"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1950052.Ender_s_Game' title='Ender's Game by Orson Scott Card' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ender's Game</a> is one of the Masterpieces of Science Fiction space opera literature. This novel, the 1st in a trilogy of prequels expands on the Formic wars, mentioned in <i>Ender's Game</i>. <br/><br/>This 1st prequel is a disappointment. My take is that it was only written to line the pockets of the authors and publishers, esp with it and its sequels coming out with the EG movie. Even this 1st book ends without being a standalone. I suspect the prequels are a single book split into 3 just to make more money. <br/><br/>All</span>
  <span id="freeText11120278428688743946" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1950052.Ender_s_Game" title="Ender's Game by Orson Scott Card" rel="nofollow noopener">Ender's Game</a> is one of the Masterpieces of Science Fiction space opera literature. This novel, the 1st in a trilogy of prequels expands on the Formic wars, mentioned in <i>Ender's Game</i>. <br /><br />This 1st prequel is a disappointment. My take is that it was only written to line the pockets of the authors and publishers, esp with it and its sequels coming out with the EG movie. Even this 1st book ends without being a standalone. I suspect the prequels are a single book split into 3 just to make more money. <br /><br />All of the EG ephemera, including comics and all sorts of collectibles underscores this opinion. Ender's Game will end up being trivialized by all the marketing and PR as was LOTR. Pity those who see the movie before reading EG and Speaker for the Dead... <br /><br />As ordinary Solar System space opera it is readable, just nothing special. It requires no thought and lacks the gray ethical/moral conflicts in the original novel. 'Tis sad. <br /><br />An aside— Since learning of Card's extreme homophobia, I only have acquired used books to avoid giving any money to Card and will do so when used DVD's of the movie become available, even if more expensive. </span>

<div id="review_360305666" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/360305666" />
    <a title="Ian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8698328-ian"><img alt="Ian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339422007p2/8698328.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/360305666?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/8698328-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer360305666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11406231375167795108">This novel began as a graphic novel in the increasingly bloated and now franchised series that began with _Ender's Game_, and it has all the strengths and weaknesses of a graphic novel: a page-turning plot and incredibly shallow characters and setting. <br/><br/>Though billed as the work of Orson Scott Card, the book is in fact a collaboration with Aaron Johnston, and the writing is consequently spotty. There are passages that sound like Card, with his characteristic tense dialogue and sense of character,</span>
  <span id="freeText11406231375167795108" style="display:none">This novel began as a graphic novel in the increasingly bloated and now franchised series that began with _Ender's Game_, and it has all the strengths and weaknesses of a graphic novel: a page-turning plot and incredibly shallow characters and setting. <br /><br />Though billed as the work of Orson Scott Card, the book is in fact a collaboration with Aaron Johnston, and the writing is consequently spotty. There are passages that sound like Card, with his characteristic tense dialogue and sense of character, but there are other parts where the writing is embarrassingly simplistic and the editing shoddy. It is heavily reminiscent of other science fiction. The simple setting and action remind me of early sci-fi potboilers like the _Venus Equilateral_ or _Skylark of Valeron_, while the depiction of the free miner ship borrows heavily from Robert Heinlein's depiction of the free traders in _Citizen of the Galaxy_.<br /><br />Overall, the story will appeal to the inner twelve-year-old boy (thus, I read avidly to the end). Don't expect it to match up to the first books of the _Ender's Game_ series and you won't be disappointed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11406231375167795108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1028122973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3637643150997114028">Start of a prequel series to Card's big hit <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/375802.Ender_s_Game__The_Ender_Quintet___1_' title='Ender's Game (The Ender Quintet, #1) by Orson Scott Card' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ender's Game</a>, and not a self-contained story but rather the hook for the series. Prequels are difficult since the reader usually knows where they're going, though Card left some room to fill in details and characters. Humanity in this case is represented by tightknit clans of cantankerous asteroid miners and a nasty, evil corporation. (Plus the introduction of a super-elite military special ops unit that's irrelevant to the events in this novel, but pr</span>
  <span id="freeText3637643150997114028" style="display:none">Start of a prequel series to Card's big hit <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/375802.Ender_s_Game__The_Ender_Quintet___1_" title="Ender's Game (The Ender Quintet, #1) by Orson Scott Card" rel="nofollow noopener">Ender's Game</a>, and not a self-contained story but rather the hook for the series. Prequels are difficult since the reader usually knows where they're going, though Card left some room to fill in details and characters. Humanity in this case is represented by tightknit clans of cantankerous asteroid miners and a nasty, evil corporation. (Plus the introduction of a super-elite military special ops unit that's irrelevant to the events in this novel, but presumably will play a part somewhere in the prequel trilogy (?)).<br /><br /> The characters include a mix of Card's child prodigies and a few grizzled veterans to dispense hard-won wisdom.<br /><br /> I just didn't feel an engagement with the PoV characters, and the outcome of their efforts is pretty much foreordained.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3637643150997114028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WwnrOCBDhUHvl8w3xBSYSlwyBj3VHp88m+t/16yAFIqmXq4QAZzZCSPxy7jSzOxq+2Y+sLuOF7BvGVavk7DrGQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Sa0kdA8OT8JtKld0cc37h8ef66aYlML/8VGFNdwlQW+0+mFcLtETiqFMUPtnFY+nYMvTK/YESnMFo6xN4xW+/A==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2677040944111012616">Orson Scott Card is the author of the novels <i>Ender's Game</i>, <i>Ender's Shadow</i>, and <i>Speaker for the Dead</i>, which are widely read by adults and younger readers, and are increasingly used in schools.<br/><br/>Besides these and other science fiction novels, Card writes contemporary fantasy (<i>Magic Street</i>, <i>Enchantment</i>, <i>Lost Boys</i>), biblical novels (<i>Stone Tables</i>, <i>Rachel and Leah</i>), the American frontier fantasy series Th</span>
  <span id="freeText2677040944111012616" style="display:none">Orson Scott Card is the author of the novels <i>Ender's Game</i>, <i>Ender's Shadow</i>, and <i>Speaker for the Dead</i>, which are widely read by adults and younger readers, and are increasingly used in schools.<br /><br />Besides these and other science fiction novels, Card writes contemporary fantasy (<i>Magic Street</i>, <i>Enchantment</i>, <i>Lost Boys</i>), biblical novels (<i>Stone Tables</i>, <i>Rachel and Leah</i>), the American frontier fantasy series The Tales of Alvin Maker (beginning with <i>Seventh Son</i>), poetry (<i>An Open Book</i>), and many plays and scripts.<br /><br />Card was born in Washington and grew up in California, Arizona, and Utah. He served a mission for the LDS Church in Brazil in the early 1970s. Besides his writing, he teaches occasional classes and workshops and directs plays. He recently began a long-term position as a professor of writing and literature at Southern Virginia University.<br /><br />Card currently lives in Greensboro, North Carolina, with his wife, Kristine Allen Card, and their youngest child, Zina Margaret.<br /><br /><i>For further details, see the author's <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orson_Scott_Card" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia</a> page.<br />For an ordered list of the author's works, see Wikipedia's <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_works_by_Orson_Scott_Card" rel="nofollow noopener">List of works by Orson Scott Card</a>.</i><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/orsonscottcard">http://us.macmillan.com/author/orsons...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2677040944111012616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
